<span id="freeTextContainer16024354104988741689">Aubrey Wallace is the kind of man no one notices. Dotty Johnson is the kind of woman no one can ingore. One afternoon, they both disappear from the small Vermont town where they live. The next day, two hundred miles away, a toddler is snatched from her Massachusetts home.For the next five years, Aubrey, Dotty, and the kidnapped child<strong>—</strong>bound together by strange love and desp</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16024354104988741689">Aubrey Wallace is the kind of man no one notices. Dotty Johnson is the kind of woman no one can ingore. One afternoon, they both disappear from the small Vermont town where they live. The next day, two hundred miles away, a toddler is snatched from her Massachusetts home.For the next five years, Aubrey, Dotty, and the kidnapped child<strong>—</strong>bound together by strange love and desperate need<strong>—</strong>are trapped in a nomadic existence governed by their constant fear of discovery. Canny, the little girl, becomes Aubrey's entire existence. But Dotty wants out. She is tired of being saddled with this fearful little man. When she meets Jiggy Huller, a brutal ex-convict, the wheels of Canny's return to her natural parents are wrenched fatally into motion.</span>

<span id="freeTextContainer6727199274922088919"><p> 4.5 Stars, buy it </p> <br /><p> Self Purchase for Kindle. </p> <br /><p> First Impression: Weird as usual. </p> <br />3rd issue is particularly confusing. 4th is less confusing but rather boring, just a kid talking to a ghost but it becomes a bit on the scary side as the bad side of Zack makes an appearance.   <span style="display:none" id="freeText6727199274922088919"><p>
  4.5 Stars,  buy it
</p> <br /><p>
  Self Purchase for Kindle.
</p> <br /><p>
  First Impression: Weird as usual. 
</p> <br />3rd issue is particularly confusing. 4th is less confusing but rather boring, just a kid talking to a ghost but it becomes a bit on the scary side as the bad side of Zack makes an appearance. Kinsey admits to Zack she loves him- That is not going to end well.Tyler appears to be close to figuring out that Zack is not what he seems. It only took 4 volumes, but I’m finally starting to get used to the art work. The squished faces aren’t bothering me anymore. The first two issues i was bored and confused but the last two issues were fantastic and ends at an intense point. It’s not a cliffhanger per say but it leaves you screaming for more!! And I don’t normally like horror type stuff but this series really is fantastic.  Not for kids unless they are older teenagers. But really good, worth buying. Maybe I won’t wait so long to read the next volume but I have so much waiting."</span>

        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it">really liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="really liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer161955877">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer9459469714990050501">John Steinbeck begins setting his novels in the 1980's and writing under a female pen-name. I couldn't stop reading, but it was like watching a train wreck. So well-written, I couldn't look away, even though I knew I was going to be so depressed along the way and when I was finished. Not an uplifting read: almost a horror-story. But an amazing feat of authorship. I'd read Morris again, but only after I've had a little light-heartedness. </span>

          </span>
        </div>

<div itemtype="http://schema.org/Review" itemscope="" itemprop="reviews" class="review" id="review_502772262">
  <link href="http://www.goodreads.com/review/show/502772262" itemprop="url" />
  <a href="/user/show/2557620-linda" class="left imgcol" title="Linda"><img src="http://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" alt="Linda" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/502772262?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 10, 2013</a>

      <a href="/user/show/2557620-linda" class="user" title="Linda">Linda</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>



        


    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer502772262">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer16104737592051432533">If you are a fan of Irene Hannon, you are in for one power-packed suspense story!<br /><br />Reporter Moira Harrison finds herself lost in a torrential downpour on Highway 94 out of Augusta. Though not technically needing glasses to drive, she reaches for her purse to find them. The purse gets hooked, and she glances over for just a second to find them. Upon returning her eyes back to the road, a woman is in the middle of the road waving for her to stop. Hydroplaning and losing control, she ends up hitting</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText16104737592051432533">If you are a fan of Irene Hannon, you are in for one power-packed suspense story!<br /><br />Reporter Moira Harrison finds herself lost in a torrential downpour on Highway 94 out of Augusta. Though not technically needing glasses to drive, she reaches for her purse to find them. The purse gets hooked, and she glances over for just a second to find them. Upon returning her eyes back to the road, a woman is in the middle of the road waving for her to stop. Hydroplaning and losing control, she ends up hitting the woman and slamming into a tree, causing her temple to impact the side window.<br /><br />She reaches to find her phone to call 911 when she hears a male voice asking her if she was okay. He cautions her to watch for glass as she searches. She feels a jab on her thigh, and the man brushes off the glass. He tells her that he’ll call 911 and go check on the woman. But both he and the woman disappear.<br /><br />She’s dizzy and passes out, awakening an hour later. With no emergency help there, she calls 911. Upon their arrival she tells what happened, but they find no evidence of a woman getting hit, and claim she must have hit a deer.<br /><br />Knowing she didn’t hit a deer, she asks an ex-homicide private detective, Cal Burke, at Phoenix Inc., to check out her story. But upon meeting the receptionist, she’s having second thoughts. Reluctantly, the Phoenix group takes her case pro bono, with Call as lead investigator.<br /><br />This is where the story takes on multiple, mind-bending twists and scenarios, with Moira’s life ending up in danger. Someone wants her silent! And it’s mostly Cal’s job to keep her safe. Their budding romance sizzles between the dangerous scenarios and circumstances. But don’t be fooled by the romance; this is one power-packed book of suspense that keeps the pages flying to the end.<br /><br />As always, Irene’s characters are real and complex, making for a tight, riveting story. The suspenseful twists are mind-boggling and a challenge to figure out before the end of the story. I’m certainly looking forward to her second in the Private Justice series coming out in the Fall of 2013!<br /><br />This book was provided by Donna Hausler, Publicity Assistant/Blog Tour Coordinator, of Baker Publishing Group. No monetary compensation was received.</span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="16104737592051432533">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a href="/review/show/143768929?book_show_action=true" itemprop="publishDate" class="reviewDate createdAt right">Jan 26, 2011</a>

      <a href="/user/show/4860627-darryl-mexic" class="user" title="Darryl Mexic">Darryl Mexic</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it">liked it</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span><span class="staticStar p0" size="15x15" title="liked it"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer143768929">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4840852751329606828"> “Vanished” by Mary McGarry Morris is Ms. Morris’ first novel. Although I have greatly enjoyed several of Ms. Morris’ later novels, I was disappointed in this one. The novel could have been titled, “White Trash”. Such trashy people are hardly imaginable. Aubrey Wallace is barely above retarded, in an awful marriage with two children and a dead end job on a work gang building and improving roads in Vermont. He ends up with a young and good looking runaway, who kidnaps an eighteen month old baby g</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText4840852751329606828"> “Vanished” by Mary McGarry Morris is Ms. Morris’ first novel. Although I have greatly enjoyed several of Ms. Morris’ later novels, I was disappointed in this one. The novel could have been titled, “White Trash”. Such trashy people are hardly imaginable. Aubrey Wallace is barely above retarded, in an awful marriage with two children and a dead end job on a work gang building and improving roads in Vermont. He ends up with a young and good looking runaway, who kidnaps an eighteen month old baby girl and runs off with Aubrey. They move from town to town and job to job, including petty thievery, living as a family, with Dotty completely controlling Aubrey and both loving “their” little girl, Canny, until five years later, Dotty decides to give Canny back to her family in hopes of collecting a reward and moving on to a chance of a lifetime in Hollywood. It all turns out tragically for Aubrey, who never wanted anything other than to be loved and to hurt no one. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="4840852751329606828">...more</a>

          </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars"><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing">it was amazing</span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span><span class="staticStar p10" size="15x15" title="it was amazing"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span style="" class="readable" id="reviewTextContainer601346191">
            
<span id="freeTextContainer12046036751521244618">This was a powerful book! Take equal parts of <a title="The Grapes of Wrath by John Steinbeck" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4395.The_Grapes_of_Wrath">The Grapes of Wrath</a> and <a title="Tobacco Road by Erskine Caldwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59091.Tobacco_Road">Tobacco Road</a> with a psycho-criminal plot to it and combine it in less than 250 pages! I've read others of Morris' books and this was a strong debut novel. Characters were defined strongly and as for the details of food, dress, travel--let's just say I couldn't stop scratching my head reading the description of nits! Both Dottie and Aubrie are unreliable narrators so the reader doesn't really know who to trust. Was Aubrie reall</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText12046036751521244618">This was a powerful book! Take equal parts of <a title="The Grapes of Wrath by John Steinbeck" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/4395.The_Grapes_of_Wrath">The Grapes of Wrath</a> and <a title="Tobacco Road by Erskine Caldwell" href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/59091.Tobacco_Road">Tobacco Road</a> with a psycho-criminal plot to it and combine it in less than 250 pages! I've read others of Morris' books and this was a strong debut novel. Characters were defined strongly and as for the details of food, dress, travel--let's just say I couldn't stop scratching my head reading the description of nits! Both Dottie and Aubrie are unreliable narrators so the reader doesn't really know who to trust. Was Aubrie really that slow and Dottie really that smart? Who knows? </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="12046036751521244618">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked &amp;&amp; exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;name=' + shelf_name + '&amp;a=' + action + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('6l1fdh2rx1sXyWx/6QnlISsOLZRphWRzPWBEdVbXgr6PiWCl73nToZsRGMSXaAOTYvnujSBYI9lXaUHnmkJ0+w==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&amp;book_id=' + book_id + '&amp;refresh=true' + '&amp;authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('ArKfW9cTGO0xzruNJzJDaeTJLhZGv+qLbWRVaJgKHoRnZqCIJcEMF70WzzZZU6XbrT7tDw9irSEHbVD6VJ/owQ==')})
  }

Their days are spent performing a ritual of prayer and storytelling, as they knit the wool of the sheep who inhabit the monastery grounds and into whose bodies they believe their deceased sisters\' souls to have entered. Then, one day, seemingly out of nowhere, a priest appears. Hoping to rise in the church hierarchy, he has presented plans to his bishop to convert what he believes is an uninhabited and valuable piece of church property into a spa for the wealthy-and he has come to investigate the land. Father Ignatius is as surprised to see the nuns as they are to see a flesh-and-blood man, and what follows is the strange, moving, and often hilarious story of their struggle-a struggle of wills, but also of faith. Lambs of God is a beautifully written and haunting story of colliding traditions, conflicting beliefs, and magical trans-formations. It weaves together Christian belief, classical mythology, fairy tales, Celtic lore, and the mysteries of the natural world into one of the most memorable and gripping of contemporary novels. Like Ron Hansen\'s Mariette in Ecstasy, Lambs of God is a wildly original investigation into the nature and complexities of faith.&lt;\/span&gt;\n  &lt;a data-text-id=\"11711624508875156834\" Yet his life is overturned in the winter of 1846, when his Nez Perce wife deserts him and his children die of smallpox. In the grip of a profound sorrow, MacLaren, whose home once spanned a continent, sets out to find his wife. But an act of secret vengeance changes his course, introducing him to a different wife and mother: Lucy Mitchell, journeying westward with her family.Lucy, a remarried widow, careful mother, and reluctant emigrant, is drawn at once to the self-possessed MacLaren. Convinced that he is the key to her family’s safe passage, she persuades her husband to employ him. As their hidden stories and obsessions unfold, and pasts and cultures collide, both Lucy and MacLaren must confront the people they have truly been, are, and may become.Alive with incident and insight, presenting with rare scope and intimacy the complex relations among nineteenth-century traders, immigrants, and Native Americans, A Sudden Country is, above all, a heroic and unforgettable     <div class=" clearFloats bigBox" id="aboutAuthor"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground"><a href="/author/show/3522.Mary_McGarry_Morris">About Mary McGarry Morris</a></h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent">
    <div class="readable">
      
<span id="freeTextContainer9979562280465138586">As the author of several novels, <em>Mary McGarry Morris</em> has received considerable attention from critics and readers, as well as from prestigious awards panels. <br />Her books are noted for their depictions of mentally and emotionally impaired individuals who have difficulty coping with an inhospitable world. <br />As New York Times Book Review contributor <em>Alice McDermott</em> put it, “Morris does not devise plots,</span>
  <span style="display:none" id="freeText9979562280465138586">As the author of several novels, <em>Mary McGarry Morris</em> has received considerable attention from critics and readers, as well as from prestigious awards panels. <br />Her books are noted for their depictions of mentally and emotionally impaired individuals who have difficulty coping with an inhospitable world. <br />As New York Times Book Review contributor <em>Alice McDermott</em> put it, “Morris does not devise plots, but traps: steel-toothed, inescapable traps of circumstance and personality against which her characters struggle... and then fail.” Ultimately, Morris suggests that these individuals are incapable of surviving their surroundings. <br />Her books typically conclude with violent murders, death apparently being all that is left for characters who have exhausted their other possibilities. </span>
  <a onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;" href="#" data-text-id="9979562280465138586">...more</a>

    </div>
